## Day 32 — 20:00 — Quota Alert Notifications: webhook-based proactive warning when monthly quota crosses threshold (3010 backend + 1577 frontend = 4587 tests)

No community issues today. All spec phases remain 100% complete. This session identified a genuine Track D gap: analysts who configure a monthly quota (built Day 31, 04:00) have no early warning before their VP's prediction dashboard starts returning 429 errors — they only know the quota is exhausted after it's too late. The vision's "Fail gracefully — always suggest next steps" principle applies to operators too, not just end-users. An analyst who has shared a model URL with their developer or VP needs a heads-up when usage is climbing toward the limit so they can increase it before it bites.

**What was built:** `quota_alert_threshold_pct: Optional[int]` field on `Deployment` (backward-compatible `None` default; inline SQLite migration). `EVENT_QUOTA_ALERT = "quota_alert"` added to `core/webhook.py` `ALL_EVENTS` (4 event types total). `_check_and_fire_quota_alert(deployment_id, used, quota, threshold_pct)` pure helper in `api/deploy.py`: fires a `quota_alert` webhook dispatch exactly when `used == ceil(quota * threshold / 100)` — the precise prediction that first crosses the boundary — preventing repeated alerts on every subsequent prediction above the threshold. Dispatched in a background daemon thread so prediction latency is unaffected. `PUT /api/deploy/{id}/quota-alert` endpoint: validates 1-99 range (0 or null removes alert; negative or >99 → 422); returns `quota_alert_enabled`, `quota_alert_threshold_pct`, `monthly_quota`, and a plain-English message. `GET /api/deploy/{id}/quota-status` extended with `quota_alert_threshold_pct` and `quota_alert_enabled`. `_QUOTA_ALERT_PATTERNS` regex (8 NL variants: "alert me when I hit 80% of my quota", "notify me when my quota is almost full", "set a quota alert at 90%", "configure quota alert", "alert me at 85", "disable the quota alert", "quota alert threshold", "quota usage alert") in `chat.py`. Handler reads/sets the threshold via `Deployment.quota_alert_threshold_pct`, computes current usage, emits `{type:"quota_alert_config"}` SSE event. Claude's system prompt injected with threshold summary and narration instructions. `QuotaAlertCard` (orange border, 🔔 icon): "Alert at X%"/"Disabled" badge, explanation paragraph ("You will receive a webhook notification when usage reaches X%"), current usage fraction + color-coded `UsageBar` (green/amber/red at 70%/90%), remaining predictions, help-text footer. One fix during implementation: regex arm `(?:alert|warn|notify)\s+...%` failed word-boundary because `%` is non-word — fixed by dropping the `%` suffix from that arm (digit provides the boundary). Pre-existing test `test_all_events_constant_has_three_entries` updated to `has_expected_entries` (now 4 event types).

**Testing:** 7 `PUT /api/deploy/{id}/quota-alert` tests (set 80, set 90, remove with 0, remove with null, invalid negative, invalid >99, 404) + 2 quota-status tests (alert fields present when disabled, reflects set alert) + 3 `_check_and_fire_quota_alert` pure-logic tests (fires exactly at crossing/no fire before/no fire after, no fire when below threshold, payload contains expected fields) + 9 `_QUOTA_ALERT_PATTERNS` detection tests (7 positive, 2 negative) = 21 backend; 16 frontend (region aria-label, 🔔 icon aria-hidden, heading, Alert at N% badge, Disabled badge, threshold explanation, usage fraction, pct_used, progressbar, remaining text, summary text, help text, no usage bar without quota, store attach on assistant, no-attach on user, no-crash on empty). **21 backend + 16 frontend = 37 new tests. Total: 3010 backend + 1577 frontend = 4587, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend lint: clean.**

## Day 31 — 20:00 — Partial Dependence Plots via chat: marginal effect averaged over training data (2961 backend + 1527 frontend = 4488 tests)

No community issues today. All spec phases remain 100% complete. This session implemented **Partial Dependence Plots (PDP) via chat** — a Track C (Model Building Depth) feature that fills a genuine gap between sensitivity analysis and the vision's "Not a black box" promise. Sensitivity analysis sweeps one feature while holding all others at their training means — a useful first approximation, but it ignores the actual distribution of training data. For example, if "units" is always high when "region" is "East", holding "region" at its mean produces a misleading sensitivity curve. PDPs average over the actual training rows, giving a more statistically accurate marginal effect estimate.

**What was built:** `compute_partial_dependence(model, X_train, feature_idx, grid_values, problem_type, class_names)` pure function in `core/explainer.py` — for each grid value, replaces the feature column across all training rows and averages predictions. Regression uses `model.predict()`; binary classification uses `predict_proba()[:, 1]`; multiclass builds per-class probability curves. Returns `{grid_values, mean_predictions, std_predictions, class_curves, n_training_rows, summary}` with a plain-English summary describing trend direction and magnitude. `GET /api/models/{run_id}/partial-dependence?feature=&steps=20` endpoint in `api/validation.py` (400 on unknown feature, 404 on missing run; steps clamped 5–50; constant-feature → single grid point). `_PDP_PATTERNS` (8 NL variants: "partial dependence for X", "PDP for X", "marginal effect of X", "average effect of X on the prediction", "population-level effect of X", "partial dependence plot for X") + `_detect_pdp_feature()` longest-match scanner in `chat.py`. Chat handler picks the best/selected completed run, computes PDP, injects trend summary into system prompt so Claude narrates the marginal effect in plain English, emits `{type:"partial_dependence"}` SSE event. `PartialDependenceCard` (purple border, 📉 icon): trend badge (↑ Increases / ↓ Decreases / → Flat), algorithm badge, italic "averaged over N training records" explainer distinguishing PDP from sensitivity, Recharts LineChart with purple mean line + violet dashed ±1 std band; multiclass shows per-class curves with colour legend; constant-feature shows fallback message instead of empty chart. `PartialDependenceResult` TypeScript type; `partial_dependence?` on `ChatMessage`; `attachPartialDependenceToLastMessage` Zustand action; SSE handler and render wired in workspace page.

**Testing:** 4 pattern detection tests + 2 `_detect_pdp_feature()` tests + 11 `compute_partial_dependence()` pure-function tests (regression keys, grid length, trend direction, n_training_rows, summary text, binary classification probabilities in range, no class_curves for binary, multiclass class_curves with 3 classes, each curve length matches grid, constant feature single point, problem_type preserved) + 5 API integration tests + 3 Zustand store action tests + 12 `PartialDependenceCard` component tests = **29 backend + 15 frontend = 44 new tests. Total: 2961 backend + 1527 frontend = 4488, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend build + lint: clean.**

## Day 31 — 12:00 — Prediction Input Guard Rails: out-of-range + unknown-category warnings (2932 backend + 1512 frontend = 4444 tests)

No community issues today. All spec phases remain 100% complete. This session addressed a genuine gap in the "Not a black box" and "Fail gracefully" vision promises: when a VP or analyst enters a prediction input far outside the model's training distribution (e.g., revenue=$10M when training data ranged $500–$5K, or region="Atlantis" which never appeared in training), AutoModeler was silently producing a prediction with no caveat — potentially misleading.

**What was built:** `feature_ranges: dict` field added to `PredictionPipeline` (backward-compatible `field(default_factory=dict)`, so old pipeline files load without error). At pipeline build time in `build_prediction_pipeline()`, numeric features now record `{p5, p95, min, max}` and categorical features record `{known_categories: list[str]}`. `validate_prediction_inputs(provided_features, pipeline)` pure function in `core/deployer.py` checks ONLY the features explicitly provided by the user (not defaults), returning a list of `{feature, provided_value, severity, expected_min, expected_max, training_min, training_max, message}` dicts for numeric violations or `{feature, provided_value, severity, known_categories, message}` for unknown categories. Three severity levels: `out_of_range` (outside p5–p95 typical range), `extreme_outlier` (outside absolute min–max), and `unknown_category`. `predict_single()` gained an optional `provided_features` kwarg; when supplied, calls the validator and includes `guard_rail_warnings` in the return dict (omitted when empty, so the API response is unchanged for well-behaved inputs). `make_prediction()` in `api/deploy.py` passes `provided_features=input_data` (the user's raw request body). The chat inline prediction handler now passes `_ip_extracted` (the features extracted from the user's message, before defaults are merged) as `provided_features`, and injects a plain-English warning summary into the Claude system prompt addendum so Claude mentions the caveat in its narration.

**Frontend:** `GuardRailWarning` TypeScript interface (`feature, provided_value, severity, message, expected_min?, expected_max?, training_min?, training_max?, known_categories?`) added to `types.ts`. `InlinePredictionResult` and `PredictionResult` gain `guard_rail_warnings?: GuardRailWarning[]`. `InlinePredictionCard` updated: when warnings are present, the card border shifts from blue to amber, a warning-count badge appears in the header, and each warning renders as a `role="alert"` row with severity label (Out of range / Extreme outlier / Unknown category), the full message, and either the typical training range (numeric) or up to 5 known categories (categorical). Public `predict/[id]/page.tsx` result section renders a compact amber warning callout block below the confidence badge. `GuardRailWarning` imported in `predict/[id]/page.tsx` for typed map.

**Testing:** 12 `validate_prediction_inputs` unit tests (in-range numeric→no warning, out-of-range→warning, extreme outlier below min, unknown category→warning, known category→no warning, multiple warnings, empty provided features, None value skipped, feature_ranges stored in pipeline, categorical known_categories stored, predict_single with warnings, predict_single no warnings when provided_features=None) + 5 API integration tests (in-range→no warnings, extreme units→warnings, unknown region→warning, warnings include message, warning dict structure). 17 frontend tests across no-warning and warning scenarios (aria-label, no-warning badge, prediction value, warning count badge singular/plural, out-of-range message, extreme outlier message, unknown category message, typical range shown, known categories shown, severity labels for all three types, prediction still shows with warnings, aria-label on warnings section, role=alert per row, empty array shows no warnings). **17 backend + 17 frontend = 34 new tests. Total: 2932 backend + 1512 frontend = 4444, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend build + lint: clean.**

## Day 31 — 04:00 — Per-Deployment Rate Limiting + Monthly Quotas (2915 backend + 1495 frontend = 4410 tests)

No community issues today. The spec is 100% complete across all phases and tracks. This session addressed one of the last missing table-stakes features for production-grade deployed prediction endpoints: rate limiting and monthly quota management. Without these, any analyst sharing a model URL risks runaway API usage — either accidental (a buggy integration polling thousands of times per minute) or intentional (quota exhaustion from an external party). Business analysts don't think in terms of RPM windows or rolling 30-day counts; they think "I want my model to handle at most 60 requests per minute and 1000 predictions this month."

**What was built:** Two new optional fields on the `Deployment` SQLModel: `rate_limit_rpm` (Optional[int], per-minute cap) and `monthly_quota` (Optional[int], rolling 30-day prediction count cap). Both added via inline SQLite `ALTER TABLE` migrations in `db.py` (the established no-downtime migration pattern). `_check_rate_limit(deployment_id, rpm)` — sliding window using a `deque` per deployment key in an in-memory `dict` protected by `threading.Lock`; timestamps are `time.monotonic()` so they're immune to wall-clock drift; entries older than 60 seconds are evicted on each call; returns False when the window already contains `>= rpm` entries. `_check_monthly_quota(deployment, session)` — counts `PredictionLog` rows for this deployment where `created_at >= now - 30 days`; returns `(allowed: bool, used: int, quota: int)`. Both checks run inside `make_prediction()` after API key verification; HTTP 429 is raised with a plain-English message describing which limit was hit. `PUT /api/deploy/{id}/rate-limit` sets/clears both limits atomically (0 → store None; explicit null → store None). `GET /api/deploy/{id}/quota-status` returns `{quota_enabled, monthly_quota, used_this_month, remaining, pct_used, rate_limit_rpm, rate_limit_enabled, summary}`. `GET /api/deploy/{id}` deployment detail now exposes both fields. `_rate_limit_summary()` helper composes the plain-English summary string.

Chat integration follows the established SSE card pattern. `_RATE_LIMIT_PATTERNS` regex (7 arms, 8+ NL variants) detects set/enable/configure/disable/remove/check intents. `_RATE_LIMIT_NUMBER_RE` and `_QUOTA_NUMBER_RE` extract numeric targets from the message. `_DISABLE_RATE_RE` and `_DISABLE_QUOTA_RE` detect removal intents. The handler block applies the DB change, computes current usage, and builds a `rate_limit_event` dict — then injects a system prompt addendum so Claude narrates the change in plain English. SSE emits `{type: "rate_limit", rate_limit: {...}}`. `RateLimitCard` (amber border, ⚡ icon, role="region") shows: "Active"/"No limits" badge; per-minute limit or "Unlimited"; monthly quota fraction ("450 / 1,000"), color-coded `UsageBar` (green < 70%, amber 70–90%, red ≥ 90%), percentage used, remaining predictions; help text footer for updating via chat. `attachRateLimitToLastMessage` Zustand action attaches to the last assistant message only. `RateLimitInfo` + `QuotaStatus` TypeScript interfaces added to `types.ts`; `setRateLimit()` and `quotaStatus()` methods added to `api.deploy`.

**Testing:** 26 backend integration tests: `PUT /rate-limit` (set RPM, set quota, set both, remove with 0, remove with null, negative rejected 422, 404 not found), `GET /quota-status` (no limits, with quota, with RPM, 404), `GET /deploy/{id}` (fields present, fields reflect set limits), `POST /predict` (allowed under quota), `_check_rate_limit()` pure-function tests (first request allowed, blocks on exceed, allows after window expires), `_RATE_LIMIT_PATTERNS` (set RPM phrase, enable, monthly quota, quota status, check quota, disable, remove quota, unrelated phrase). 17 frontend tests: region aria-label, heading, "No limits" badge, "Active" badge, rpm value, "Unlimited" for absent rpm, quota fraction, percentage, remaining, progress bar aria-valuenow, both limits, summary text, help text, aria-hidden emoji, store attach on assistant, no-attach on user, empty messages no-op. **26 backend + 17 frontend = 43 new tests. Total: 2915 backend + 1495 frontend = 4410, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend build + lint: clean.**

## Day 30 — 20:00 — Cross-Project Portfolio Overview: "show all my models" card (2889 backend + 1478 frontend = 4367 tests)

No community issues today. The spec is 100% complete across all phases and tracks. This session identified a genuine cross-cutting gap: analysts who manage multiple AutoModeler projects (a churn model, a revenue forecast, a demand prediction) had no way to get a bird's-eye view of all their work in a single chat message. They'd have to navigate between projects manually to compare model performance, check deployment status, or see total prediction counts. The Cross-Project Portfolio Overview feature closes this gap.

**What was built:** `compute_portfolio_summary(project_summaries)` pure function in `core/analyzer.py` — accepts a list of per-project summary dicts (project_id, name, dataset, model_count, best_algorithm, best_metric_name, best_metric_value, problem_type, target_column, has_deployment, prediction_count, last_activity_at), returns: total_projects, active_deployments, total_predictions, best_performer (project with highest metric value; None if no models), projects list, and a plain-English summary sentence. `GET /api/projects/portfolio` endpoint in `api/projects.py` — registered BEFORE the `/{project_id}` wildcard route (critical: FastAPI matches routes in registration order, so a `/portfolio` literal must precede `/{project_id}` or "portfolio" gets interpreted as a project ID); endpoint queries all projects, finds best model run + active deployment + prediction count per project, calls `compute_portfolio_summary()`. `_PORTFOLIO_PATTERNS` regex in `chat.py` (10 NL variants: "show all my models", "portfolio overview", "portfolio summary", "compare all my projects", "which project is doing best", "cross-project view", "all my work", etc.); handler cross-queries all projects from the session (not just the current project — unique among all chat handlers), builds project summaries inline, injects summary into system prompt, emits `{type:"portfolio"}` SSE event. `PortfolioCard` (purple border, 🗂️ icon): header row with project count badge, deployed count badge, total predictions badge; plain-English summary paragraph; 🏆 "Best Performer" emerald highlight box naming the top-metric project + algorithm + target column + metric%; per-project rows (project name, dataset filename + row count, target column + algorithm, metric badge, Live/Trained/No model status badge, prediction count). One bug caught during implementation: the `/portfolio` route was returning 404 because it was registered after `/{project_id}` — fixed by moving the portfolio endpoint block above the wildcard route. `PortfolioResult`/`PortfolioProjectSummary`/`PortfolioBestPerformer` TypeScript interfaces; `portfolio?` field added to `ChatMessage`; `attachPortfolioToLastMessage` Zustand action; SSE handler + render wired in workspace page.

**Testing:** 10 `_PORTFOLIO_PATTERNS` detection tests + 8 `compute_portfolio_summary` unit tests (empty list, total_projects, active_deployments, total_predictions, best_performer selected correctly by max metric, best_performer None when no models, summary text includes key facts, projects list returned) + 3 API endpoint tests (200 OK, empty DB → zero projects, with project → project in response) = 21 backend; 16 frontend (aria-label region, heading, 0 projects badge, empty state message, 1 project badge, deployed badge, predictions badge, best performer section, best performer name, metric %, multi-project rows, Live badge, No model badge, 3 projects badge, store attaches on assistant message, store does not attach on user message). **21 backend + 16 frontend = 37 new tests. Total: 2889 backend + 1478 frontend = 4367, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend build + lint: clean.**

## Day 30 — 12:00 — SDK Generation: downloadable Python/JS client libraries for deployed models (2868 backend + 1462 frontend = 4330 tests)

No community issues today. The spec is 100% complete across all phases and tracks. This session found a genuine gap in the Track D (Deployment Depth) cluster: once a model is deployed as a prediction API, the analyst has no easy way to hand it to a developer. The developer would need to read API docs, figure out the endpoint shape, write HTTP code, handle errors — all friction that kills adoption. The SDK generation feature eliminates that friction: a single chat message like "generate a python sdk for my model" triggers downloadable, ready-to-use Python and JavaScript client libraries, each customized to the deployed model's feature schema, algorithm, and problem type.

**What was built:** `GET /api/deploy/{id}/sdk?language=python|javascript` endpoint in `deploy.py`. Three helper functions: `_sdk_class_name(target_column, algorithm)` → PascalCase name ("revenue" → "RevenuePredictor"); `_generate_python_sdk(...)` → full Python module with typed `predict(feature1: float, ...) → dict` and `predict_batch(rows: list[dict]) → list[dict]` methods, docstrings, requests dependency, error handling, and regression/classification-aware return-type documentation; `_generate_javascript_sdk(...)` → ES module class with `async predict(features)` and `async predictBatch(rows)` methods, JSDoc, fetch-based HTTP client. Endpoint validates language, loads deployment's `feature_names` from DB, constructs `feature_schema`, calls the appropriate generator, and returns a `Response` with `Content-Disposition: attachment; filename=...sdk.py/.js` so browsers auto-download.

`_SDK_PATTERNS` regex in `chat.py` covers 8 natural-language variants: "generate a python sdk", "download the javascript sdk", "create a python client library", "developer sdk", "how do developers use my prediction api", etc. SDK chat handler builds an `sdk_event` dict (deployment_id, target_column, algorithm, problem_type, python_url, javascript_url, class_name) and enriches the system prompt so Claude narrates the SDK in plain English. SSE emits `{type: "sdk_download", sdk_download: {...}}`. `SdkDownloadCard` frontend component (indigo border, 📦 icon, role="region"): Regression/Classification badge, algorithm label, Python and JavaScript download `<a>` links with `download` attribute, inline usage code previews for both languages, class name and method list footer. Zustand `attachSdkDownloadToLastMessage` action and page.tsx SSE handler wire the card into conversation history.

**Testing:** 8 pattern detection tests + 3 `_sdk_class_name` unit tests (basic, underscores, hyphens) + 6 `_generate_python_sdk` tests (class presence, predict methods, feature params, endpoint URL, regression doc, classification doc) + 4 `_generate_javascript_sdk` tests + 5 API endpoint integration tests (python, javascript, invalid language→400, not found→404, default language) = **27 backend**. 16 frontend tests (aria-label, heading, download links, download attribute, target column, class name, Regression badge, Classification badge, algorithm label, Python/JS usage previews, predictBatch mention, store action signature, store attach on assistant, no-attach on user). **27 backend + 16 frontend = 43 new tests. Total: 2868 backend + 1462 frontend = 4330, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend build + lint: clean.**

## Day 30 — 04:00 — Natural Language Date Range Filtering: "show Q4 2023 data", "last 6 months" (2841 backend + 1446 frontend = 4287 tests)

No community issues today. All spec items across every phase and track are fully checked. This session fixed a longstanding gap in `filter_view.py`: the docstring promised "narrow to Q4 → looks for quarter/date columns" but the actual code had zero date-specific parsing. Business analysts working with time-series data (sales, quarterly reports, monthly metrics) naturally phrase questions using time language — "show me Q4", "filter to last 6 months", "show 2023 data" — and these fell silently through the filter system.

**What was built:** `parse_date_filter_request(message, df)` pure function in `core/filter_view.py`. Date column detection by name-hint (date/time/year/month/period/quarter/week keywords) or string-value sampling — only object/string-dtype columns are sampled to avoid false-positive on numeric columns (a bug found during testing: `pd.to_datetime(100)` succeeds, treating integers as nanosecond timestamps). Resolves 6 NL patterns in priority order: (1) `last N days/weeks/months/years` relative from today; (2) `this/last year/month/quarter`; (3) `Q1–Q4` with optional year (numeric: "Q4 2023"; word: "third quarter 2023"); (4) month range ("January through March 2023"); (5) year-only ("show 2024 data"); (6) single month ("filter to March"). Returns a `date_range` operator with `{start: ISO, end: ISO}` value dict. `apply_active_filter()` extended: the `date_range` branch calls `pd.to_datetime(series, errors="coerce")` then compares timestamps (end date extended to 23:59:59 to include full day). `build_filter_summary()` formats date_range as "column between START and END". `FilterCondition` TypeScript type gains `date_range | DateRangeValue`. `FilterSetCard` renders "between START and END" via `formatConditionValue()` helper. `_FILTER_PATTERNS` regex in `chat.py` extended with date-intent phrases; chat filter handler merges `parse_date_filter_request()` results with existing field-filter results so analysts can combine ("show Q4 2023 data where region = East"). **One bug fixed during development:** numeric columns were falsely detected as date columns because `pd.to_datetime` accepts integers as nanosecond timestamps — fixed by checking `dtype == object or is_string_dtype` before sampling. **Testing:** 13 `parse_date_filter_request` unit tests (Q1 numeric, Q4, quarter word, year-only, month range, single month, last-N-months, last-N-years, this year, last year, no-date-column→None, unrelated message→None, date-col-detected-by-value) + 3 `apply_active_filter` date_range tests (Q1 filter, full year, empty result) + 1 `build_filter_summary` test = 17 backend; 5 frontend (date_range shows "between", column name, start date, end date, filtered row count). **17 backend + 5 frontend = 22 new tests. Total: 2841 backend + 1446 frontend = 4287, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend build + lint: clean.**

## Day 29 — 20:00 — Multi-Row Batch Prediction: "predict for: X; Y; Z" comparison table (2824 backend + 1441 frontend = 4265 tests)

No community issues today. All spec items across every phase and track are fully checked — 104 Phase 9 items all marked [x]. This session targeted a natural gap at the intersection of inline prediction (single row) and bulk scenario comparison (override-based): analysts who want to compare multiple independent scenarios in one shot — "predict for: Region=East Units=100; Region=West Units=150; Region=North Units=75" — and see a table result without running three separate predictions.

**What was built:** `_MULTI_ROW_PRED_PATTERNS` (6 NL variants: "batch/bulk predict for these scenarios", "run predictions for multiple records", "score these inputs", "compare these scenarios") in `chat.py`. A secondary trigger fires when any message contains `;` AND matches `_INLINE_PRED_PATTERNS` — the analyst-natural semicolon separating scenarios. `_extract_multi_row_predictions()` splits on `;`, then calls `_trim_preamble()` (finds the first known-feature key to strip leading preamble like "predict for:" before parsing) and `_extract_multi_feature_prediction()` per segment; returns non-empty list only when ≥2 rows parse successfully. Handler fires before `inline_pred_event` (mutually exclusive); runs `predict_single()` per row, builds regression range summary or classification mode summary. `MultiPredictionCard` (violet border, 📊): "Scenario Comparison" heading, count badge, Regression/Classification badge, compact HTML table (row# | prediction | up to 4 feature columns | defaults count), summary footer, defaults note. `MultiPredictionRow`/`MultiPredictionResult` TypeScript types; `attachMultiPredictionToLastMessage` Zustand action; SSE handler + render wired in `page.tsx`.

**One bug fixed during implementation:** `_extract_multi_row_predictions` initially failed on "predict for: Region=East Units=100" because `_KV_PAIR_RE` parsed "for:" → key="for", value="Region", consuming "Region" and leaving only "Units" extracted. Fixed by `_trim_preamble()`: scans each segment for the first `\bfeature_name=` match and strips everything before it, so "predict for:" disappears before parsing. **Testing:** 8 pattern tests + 6 extractor unit tests (two-row, three-row, single→empty, no-features→empty, numeric cast, mixed types) + 3 API integration tests (endpoint exists, no-deployment guard, required fields) = 17 backend; 15 frontend (aria-label, heading, count badge, regression badge, classification badge, row count, prediction values, feature column headers, summary footer, classification class+confidence, store attach/no-attach/empty). **17 backend + 15 frontend = 32 new tests. Total: 2824 backend + 1441 frontend = 4265, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend build + lint: clean.**

## Day 29 — 04:00 — Prediction Presets: "save this as a preset called Best Case" (2807 backend + 1426 frontend = 4233 tests)

No community issues today. All Phase 9 Tracks D, C, E, and the vast majority of Track B are complete. This session targeted the "VP doesn't know what to type" cold-start gap on the shared prediction dashboard. When an analyst shares the predict/[id] link, the VP opens a form with feature names like `product_category`, `region_code`, `units_sold` and has no idea what to enter. A smart colleague would have prepared a few realistic starting points — "Best Case", "Average Quarter", "Worst Case" — before handing over the link.

**What was built:** `DeploymentPreset` SQLModel table (`id`, `deployment_id`, `name`, `feature_values` JSON). `GET/POST /api/deploy/{id}/presets` + `DELETE /api/deploy/{id}/presets/{preset_id}` CRUD endpoints with validation (empty name → 422, empty feature_values → 422). Chat integration: `_PRESET_SAVE_PATTERNS` (8 NL variants: "save this as a preset called X", "add a preset called X with Y=Z", "create a prediction preset named X", "bookmark this as preset", "quick scenario called X") + `_PRESET_LIST_PATTERNS` (4 NL variants: "show my presets", "list saved scenarios", "what presets do I have"). `_extract_preset_definition()` extracts name via `called|named` lookahead regex and key=value feature pairs using `=`-only separator (avoids collision with the name separator colon). Chat handlers persist to DB via `DeploymentPreset` model and emit `{type:"preset_saved"}` + `{type:"preset_list"}` SSE events. `PresetSavedCard` (emerald border, 🎯): name, feature-count badge, `key=value` feature badges, VP hint. `PresetListCard` (indigo border, 📋): count badge, per-preset rows with feature badges + Load button. `predict/[id]/page.tsx`: `useEffect` loads presets on mount; when any exist, renders a "Quick Scenarios" pill-button row above the input form — clicking fills all inputs and clears previous result.

**One regex fix during implementation:** initial `_PRESET_KV_RE` used `(?:=|:)` for key-value separation, which caused `Best Case: Region` to be parsed as `{Case: "Region=East"}`. Fixed by switching to `=`-only, since `:` appears in name separators like "called Best Case: Region=East". **Testing:** 8 `_PRESET_SAVE_PATTERNS` tests + 4 `_PRESET_LIST_PATTERNS` tests + 5 `_extract_preset_definition()` extractor tests + 7 API integration tests (list empty, create, list after create, delete, empty name, empty features, invalid deployment) = 24 backend (1 extra for invalid deployment total = 25); 20 frontend (testid render, aria-hidden icons, preset name, feature count badge, feature value badges, VP hint, singular/plural feature, preset list testid, icon, count badge, preset rows, preset names, load buttons present/absent, load callback called, empty state, singular/plural preset, store action types). **25 backend + 20 frontend = 45 new tests. Total: 2807 backend + 1426 frontend = 4233, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend build + lint: clean.**

## Day 28 — 20:00 — Prediction Cohort Analysis + CSV Export: "who are the top predictions?" (2782 backend + 1406 frontend = 4188 tests)

No community issues today. All Phase 9 Tracks D, C, E remain complete and Track B deepens further. This session addressed two related analyst needs that follow naturally from the Dataset Ranking feature built at 12:00: (1) after getting a ranked list ("top 20 churners"), analysts ask "who ARE these people — what do they have in common?"; and (2) they need to download the list to take to their manager.

**What was built:** `compute_prediction_cohort(pipeline_path, model_path, df, n, direction)` pure function in `core/deployer.py`. Re-ranks the dataset (reuses `run_dataset_ranking`), isolates the top-N rows, and profiles them vs the full dataset. For each categorical column (≤20 unique values): computes per-category top-N% vs overall% and overrepresentation ratio. For each numeric column (excluding target): computes top-N mean vs overall mean plus direction ("higher"/"lower"/"similar") and ratio. Generates a plain-English `characterization` sentence naming the top 2 categorical and top 2 numeric distinguishing traits. Returns `{target_column, problem_type, n, direction, total_scored, categorical_profile, numeric_profile, characterization}`. `_COHORT_PATTERNS` (9 NL variants: "who are the top predictions", "what do they have in common", "profile/characterize/describe the ranked records", "cohort analysis of the ranked predictions", "tell me about the top N customers", "common traits of the top predictions") in `chat.py`; handler guarded by deployment + dataset + no ranked_pred_event already fired. `PredictionCohortCard` (indigo border, 🔍 icon): characterization paragraph at top, "Categorical Breakdown" section with dual horizontal bars (indigo=top-N group, slate=all rows), "Numeric Averages" section with per-column ratio badges (rose for much higher, amber moderate, sky lower, slate similar) + top avg vs overall avg. **CSV download:** "⬇ Download CSV" button added to `RankedPredictionsCard` — client-side `buildCsv()` generates CSV including ALL feature columns (not just the 4 shown in the table), triggers `<a download>` with `{target_column}_ranked_predictions.csv` filename.

**Testing:** 9 `_COHORT_PATTERNS` tests + 12 `compute_prediction_cohort()` pure-function tests (required fields, n/direction, target column, total_scored, categorical profile populated + has percentages, numeric profile populated + has means, characterization is string + mentions target, classification type, lowest direction) + 3 API integration tests (event emitted, required fields present, not emitted without deployment) = 24 backend; 18 frontend (aria-label, 🔍 icon aria-hidden, target column heading, Highest badge, Lowest badge, n-of-total badge, characterization text, categorical section, categorical column name, numeric section, numeric column name, empty-state message, store attach/no-attach/empty, Download CSV button present, button aria-label, download click creates blob). **24 backend + 18 frontend = 42 new tests. Total: 2782 backend + 1406 frontend = 4188, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend build + lint: clean.**

## Day 28 — 12:00 — Dataset Ranking: "which customers are most at risk?" (2758 backend + 1388 frontend = 4146 tests)

No community issues today. All Phase 9 Tracks D, C, E, and the majority of Track B are complete; this session extended Track B with **Dataset Ranking via Model** — applying a deployed model to every row in the current dataset and returning the top N ranked by prediction score. The gap: analysts who have trained and deployed a model still had no way to ask "OK, but which specific customers should I call first?" A smart colleague who just ran a churn model would immediately say "here are the 20 accounts most likely to churn — go talk to them."

**What was built:** `run_dataset_ranking(pipeline_path, model_path, df, n=20, direction="highest")` pure function in `core/deployer.py`. Loads the prediction pipeline and model, transforms the full DataFrame via `pipeline.transform_df()`, scores every row. For regression: `model.predict()` returns float scores, sorted descending or ascending per direction. For classification: `model.predict_proba()` returns class probability arrays; ranks by the max probability across classes (overall model confidence) — universally useful regardless of class names. Each ranked row includes: `rank`, `row_index`, `score`, `feature_values` (all original columns), and either `prediction` (regression) or `predicted_class + confidence + probabilities` (classification). Raises `ValueError` for empty DataFrames. Returns `{problem_type, target_column, direction, n, total_scored, rows, summary, class_names}`. `_RANKED_PRED_PATTERNS` (8 NL variants: "which customers are most likely to churn", "show me the top 20 predictions", "rank by predicted revenue", "most at risk", "best 10 opportunities", "apply the model to all my data", "bottom 5 by prediction", "top/bottom N by prediction/probability") + `_detect_ranked_pred_request(message)` extracting n (default 20, capped at 100) and direction (highest/lowest based on bottom/lowest keywords). Handler guard: fires only when deployment + dataset exist AND interaction/sensitivity/whatif/inline_prediction haven't already fired. `{type:"ranked_predictions"}` SSE event; system prompt injected with summary + narration hint. `RankedPredictionsCard` (amber border, 🏆 icon): problem type / direction / count badges; `RankBadge` sub-component (gold #1 / silver #2 / bronze #3 / gray rest); `PredictionCell` (regression: compact-formatted number; classification: "class (XX%)" with color-coded confidence — green ≥70%, amber ≥50%, red <50%); table columns: rank | prediction | up to 4 feature columns; summary footer in amber-50. `RankedPredictionRow` + `RankedPredictionsResult` TypeScript types; `attachRankedPredictionsToLastMessage` Zustand action; SSE handler and render wired in page.tsx.

**Testing:** 8 `_RANKED_PRED_PATTERNS` detection tests + 5 `_detect_ranked_pred_request()` unit tests + 8 `run_dataset_ranking()` pure-function tests (required fields, n rows returned, highest direction, lowest direction, rank numbers, classification class+confidence, summary mentions target, empty DataFrame raises) + 3 API integration tests (event emitted, required fields present, not emitted without deployment) = 24 backend; 17 frontend (aria-label, 🏆 icon aria-hidden, target column heading, count badge, Highest/Lowest badge, Regression/Classification badge, table row count, rank numbers 1/2/3, regression prediction formatting "1.5k", classification class+confidence "yes (92%)", feature column headers/values, summary footer, store attach/no-attach/empty). **24 backend + 17 frontend = 41 new tests. Total: 2758 backend + 1388 frontend = 4146, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend build + lint: clean.**

## Day 28 — 04:00 — Feature Interaction Analysis: "how do units and price interact?" (2734 backend + 1371 frontend = 4105 tests)

No community issues today. All Phase 9 Tracks D, C, E, and the large portion of Track B are complete; this session extended Track B with **Feature Interaction Analysis** — a 2-D prediction heatmap showing how two features jointly affect model output. The gap: analysts who want to find the _best combination_ of two variables ("which region+product pair yields the highest revenue?") had single-feature sensitivity sweeps (sweep one feature, hold others constant) but nothing that simultaneously varies two features. A smart colleague preparing a VP presentation would say "here's a grid showing every combination of region and product category — the top-right corner is where you want to be."

**What was built:** `run_feature_interaction(pipeline_path, model_path, feature1, feature2, base_features, n_steps=7)` pure function in `core/deployer.py`. For numeric features, sweeps `[mean − 2×std, mean + 2×std]` in n_steps points using the pipeline's stored `feature_means`/`feature_stds`. For categorical features, reads `pipeline.label_encoders[feat].classes_` to get all known values (capped at n_steps). Builds an n×m grid of predictions: for each (row_val, col_val) pair, sets `{**base_features, feature1: row_val, feature2: col_val}`, transforms via `pipeline.transform()`, and calls `model.predict()`. Regression: min/max computed from flat grid; plain-English summary names the spread % and suggests looking for the highest cell. Classification: all cells are string class labels; summary counts distinct predicted classes. Returns `{feature1, feature2, target_column, problem_type, row_labels, col_labels, values, min_val, max_val, summary}`. `_INTERACTION_PATTERNS` (8 NL variants: "interaction between X and Y", "how do X and Y interact", "joint effect of X and Y", "feature interaction heatmap", "2D sensitivity", "combined effect", "show/plot interaction", "how do X and Y affect prediction") + `_detect_interaction_request(message, feature_names)` — longest-match scan (same technique as sensitivity detector) finds two distinct feature names. Handler guards: deployment must exist; sensitivity, what-if, and inline_prediction must not have already fired. `{type:"interaction"}` SSE event; system prompt injected with summary + narration instructions. `InteractionCard` (violet border, 🔬 icon): Regression/Classification badge; min/max prediction boxes (regression only); 2-D heatmap table — corner cell shows `feat1 \ feat2` label, column headers are truncated col_labels, row headers are truncated row_labels, each data cell colored rose (low) through emerald (high) based on value's position in [min_val, max_val] range, cell title tooltip shows exact `feat1=X, feat2=Y: value`; Low/High legend strip; summary footer. Classification cells use uniform violet. `InteractionResult` TypeScript type; `attachInteractionToLastMessage` Zustand action; SSE handler and render wired in page.tsx. **Testing:** 9 pattern tests + 5 `_detect_interaction_request()` unit tests + 8 pure-function tests (regression required fields, grid dimensions, min/max present, min/max correct, summary mentions features, unknown feature ValueError, classification returns class labels, classification min/max is None) + 3 API integration tests (event emitted, required fields present, not emitted without deployment) = 25 backend; 19 frontend (aria-label, 🔬 icon aria-hidden, feature1/feature2 appear, target column appears, Regression/Classification badge, Min/Max labels for regression, no Min/Max for classification, grid table rendered, row count, column count, summary footer, color legend for regression, no legend for classification, store attach/no-attach/empty). **25 backend + 19 frontend = 44 new tests. Total: 2734 backend + 1371 frontend = 4105, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend build + lint: clean.**

## Day 27 — 20:00 — Saved Analysis Templates: "save this analysis as a template" (2684 backend + 1336 frontend = 4020 tests)

No community issues today. All Phase 9 Tracks D, C, and E remain complete; this session completed the final Track B backlog item: **Saved Analysis Templates**. The gap: analysts who ask the same questions every month (revenue by region, top products, seasonal patterns) have to retype them every time they upload new data. A smart colleague would remember what you asked last time.

**What was built:** `AnalysisTemplate` SQLModel table (`id`, `project_id`, `name`, `queries` JSON list, `created_at`). `GET/POST /api/projects/{id}/analysis-templates` + `DELETE /api/projects/{id}/analysis-templates/{tid}` CRUD endpoints with empty-name and empty-queries validation (HTTP 422). Three chat pattern groups in `chat.py` — `_SAVE_TEMPLATE_PATTERNS` (6 NL variants: "save this analysis as a template called", "create a template named", "bookmark these queries as", "save as a template", "make this a reusable template", "save my analysis workflow") + `_LIST_TEMPLATES_PATTERNS` (4 NL variants: "show my saved templates", "list my analysis templates", "what templates do I have") + `_REPLAY_TEMPLATE_PATTERNS` (6 NL variants: "replay my X template", "run my X template again", "apply my X template", "re-run my X analysis"). `_extract_template_name()` helper handles quoted names, double-quoted names, and unquoted names via a 3-group regex. Save handler: loads `Conversation` for the project, filters last 8 user messages, excludes the save-command message itself, persists as `AnalysisTemplate`, emits `{type:"template_saved"}` SSE. List handler: queries templates ordered newest-first, emits `{type:"template_list"}`. Replay handler: finds template by case-insensitive substring match of name (falls back to most recent), emits `{type:"template_replay"}` with queries as clickable buttons. `TemplateSavedCard` (emerald border, 💾): name display, query count badge (singular/plural), numbered query list, replay hint. `TemplateListCard` (blue border, 📋): count badge, per-template rows with Replay button that pre-fills chat input. `TemplateReplayCard` (purple border, ▶️): queries as click-to-send buttons — clicking auto-fills the chat input without sending, so the analyst can review/edit before running. **Testing:** 6 pattern tests + 4 name-extraction tests + 7 API integration tests = 17 backend; 17 frontend (3 card components × aria-label, icons, badges, query count, template names, callbacks). **17 backend + 17 frontend = 34 new tests. Total: 2684 backend + 1336 frontend = 4020, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend build + lint: clean.**

## Day 27 — 04:00 — Data Version History Timeline: "show my upload history" (2667 backend + 1319 frontend = 3986 tests)

No community issues today. All Phase 9 Tracks D, C, and E remain complete; this session continued Track B (Vision-Driven Innovation). The chosen gap: analysts who upload data multiple times — say, monthly sales updates — have no way to see how their data has changed across uploads. The vision says "a smart colleague... shows what it sees immediately on upload." A smart colleague would also tell you "this new data is quite different from what you trained on — you might want to retrain."

**What was built:** `compute_version_history(datasets, dataframes)` pure function in `core/analyzer.py`. Accepts a list of dataset dicts (sorted by `uploaded_at`) and corresponding DataFrames. For each consecutive pair, it calls the existing `compute_dataset_comparison()` and extracts `drift_from_previous` — a compact dict with `drift_score`, `summary`, `changed_columns`, `new_columns`, `dropped_columns`, and `row_count_change_pct`. `overall_stability` is `stable` (max drift <20), `moderate` (20–49), or `high` (≥50). Returns a `versions` list with per-version metadata plus drift info, total version count, and a plain-English summary. `GET /api/data/{project_id}/version-history` endpoint orders datasets by `uploaded_at` and returns the full history; returns 404 for unknown projects. `_VERSION_HISTORY_PATTERNS` (8 NL variants: "show my upload history", "data version timeline", "how has my data evolved", "upload history", "what datasets do I have", "show previous uploads", "history of my uploads", "data version history") in `chat.py`. Chat handler loads all project datasets, builds DataFrames, calls `compute_version_history`, injects stability + summary into the system prompt, and emits `{type:"version_history"}` SSE event. `DataVersionHistoryCard` (adaptive border matching stability, 📂 icon): stability badge (Stable emerald / Moderate Drift amber / High Drift rose) + version count header; timeline rendered latest-first; each version row shows version number circle (blue for latest with "Latest" badge), filename, date, row/column count, file size; between consecutive pairs a drift connector shows "Drift: N/100 · M cols changed · rows ±X%" with color-coded badge (green/amber/red). `DataVersionDrift`, `DataVersionEntry`, `DataVersionHistoryResult` TypeScript types; `attachVersionHistoryToLastMessage` Zustand action; SSE handler and render wired in page.tsx.

**One lint fix during implementation:** f-string without placeholders (`f"One dataset upload on record..."`) flagged by ruff — replaced with plain string. **Testing:** 9 pure-function tests (empty list, single dataset, identical datasets stable, high drift, required fields, sequential version numbers, summary present, drift fields, new/dropped columns) + 9 chat pattern tests (8 positive, 1 negative for unrelated phrase, 1 negative to confirm dataset_comparison isn't triggered by version history) + 3 API integration tests (single upload, two uploads with drift, unknown project 404). 18 frontend tests (aria-label, aria-hidden icon, version count badge, stable/moderate/high stability badges, version filenames, "Latest" badge, row count, column count, drift score, no drift connector for single version, summary text, null for empty). **22 backend + 18 frontend = 40 new tests. Total: 2667 backend + 1319 frontend = 3986, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend build + lint: clean.**

## Day 26 — 20:00 — Guided Onboarding Wizard: "guide me through this" (2645 backend + 1301 frontend = 3946 tests)

No community issues today. All Phase 9 Tracks D, C, and E remain complete; this session continued Track B (Vision-Driven Innovation). The chosen gap: business analysts who are new to AutoModeler land on a project with no guidance — they can see the chat box but don't know what the first step is. Previous sessions added proactive upload suggestions and what-can-I-do-next chips, but neither answers the explicit "walk me through this" question from a first-time user.

**What was built:** `compute_onboarding_state(has_dataset, message_count, has_target, has_model_run, has_cross_val, has_deployment)` pure function in `core/onboarding.py`. Computes progress through 6 analyst workflow steps: Upload → Explore → Set target → Train → Validate → Deploy. Each step has `title`, `description`, `hint`, `suggested_action`, `suggested_tab`, `icon`, `is_done`, `is_current`. Returns `step_index`, `completion_pct`, `current_step`, `is_complete`, `summary`. `GET /api/projects/{project_id}/onboarding` endpoint derives state from real project records — FeatureSet queried through `dataset.id` (not `project_id` since FeatureSet has no project FK). `_ONBOARDING_PATTERNS` (8 NL variants: "guide me through", "help me get started", "walk me through the steps", "show me the guide", "what should I do first", "first steps", "onboarding", "how do I use this") in `chat.py`. Chat handler computes state from `ctx` and emits `{type:"onboarding_guide"}` SSE; Claude's system prompt is injected with the current step so narration is personalized. `OnboardingGuideCard` (blue border, 🧭 icon): progress bar with `aria-progressbar`, step list with ✓/icon/○, current step description + italic hint, CTA button fires `onSwitchTab` to navigate directly to the relevant right-panel tab.

**Two bugs fixed during implementation:** (1) `done_flags[4]` was initially `has_cross_val or has_model_run`, collapsing validate and train into one step — changed to just `has_cross_val` so they remain distinct. (2) the FeatureSet query in the onboarding endpoint used `FeatureSet.project_id` which doesn't exist — fixed to query via `dataset.id`. **Testing:** 12 pure-function tests + 3 API integration tests + 11 chat pattern tests = 26 backend; 16 frontend tests (figure aria-label, 🧭 icon aria-hidden, headings, completion badge, progress bar aria-valuenow, all 6 step titles, current description, hint text, CTA callback, no CTA when null tab, checkmarks, celebrate message, store attach/no-attach/empty-list). **26 backend + 16 frontend = 42 new tests. ## Day 26 — 12:00 — Prediction Sensitivity Analysis: "how does revenue change as units varies?" (2619 backend + 1285 frontend = 3904 tests)

No community issues today. All Phase 9 Tracks D, C, and E remain complete; this session continued Track B (Vision-Driven Innovation). The chosen gap: analysts who have a deployed model can ask what-if (single value change) and inline prediction (explicit multi-feature inputs), but cannot sweep a feature continuously to see the prediction curve — a core analyst question when preparing a VP presentation ("here's the revenue sensitivity to units").

**What was built:** `run_sensitivity_analysis(pipeline_path, model_path, feature_name, sweep_values, base_features)` pure function in `core/deployer.py`. Sweeps one feature across a list of values, holds all other features at training-data means (`base_features`), calls the model for each step, and returns `{feature, target_column, problem_type, values, predictions, confidences, min_pred, max_pred, change_pct, summary}`. For regression: predictions are raw floats, change_pct is (last − first) / |first| × 100, summary names the direction and magnitude. For classification: `confidences` holds max class probability per step; when no numeric confidences, the plain table of (feature value, predicted class) is returned. `_SENSITIVITY_PATTERNS` (8 NL variants: "sensitivity analysis on/for", "how sensitive is X to Y", "sweep X from A to B", "vary X from A to B", "run a sensitivity", "how does prediction change as X varies", "effect of X on prediction", "show how X affects prediction") in `chat.py`. `_detect_sensitivity_request()` extracts feature name via longest-match scan against feature list, range (explicit "from X to Y" or defaults to ±50% around training mean), and step count (default 10). Handler guarded: fires only when deployment exists, what-if hasn't fired, and inline-prediction hasn't fired. `{type:"sensitivity"}` SSE event. `SensitivityCard` (teal border, 🎚️ icon): feature → target column heading, Regression/Classification badge, change % badge (↑ emerald / ↓ rose), min/max prediction boxes for regression, Recharts LineChart with feature value on X axis and prediction on Y axis, fallback table for classification without numeric confidences. `SensitivityResult` TypeScript type, `attachSensitivityToLastMessage` Zustand action, SSE handler and render wired in workspace page.

**One lint fix during implementation:** `_detect_sensitivity_request()` initially built `name_lower` and `name_nospace` dicts that were never used in the helper — ruff F841. Removed both. **Testing:** 8 pattern tests + 6 helper tests (explicit range, default range from mean, step count, default step count, longest-match feature, empty feature list) + 7 pure-function tests (required fields, monotonic increase, positive change_pct, min/max correct, confidences None for regression, ValueError on unknown feature, summary string) + 3 API integration tests (event emitted, required fields present, multiple data points). 17 frontend tests (aria-label, aria-hidden icon, feature name, target column, Regression badge, Classification badge, change % badge, no badge when null, min/max boxes, no min/max for classification, Recharts container regression, Recharts container with confidences, prediction table for classification, summary footer, store attach, no attach to user, empty messages). **24 backend + 17 frontend = 41 new tests. Total: 2619 backend + 1285 frontend = 3904, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend build + lint: clean.**

## Day 26 — 04:00 — Goal-Driven Training: "I need 85% accuracy" (2595 backend + 1268 frontend = 3863 tests)

No community issues today. All Phase 9 Tracks D, C, and E remain complete; this session continued Track B (Vision-Driven Innovation). The chosen gap: analysts have to manually train algorithms and compare results to find one that meets their accuracy requirement. The vision says AutoModeler should be like a smart colleague — and a smart colleague, told "I need 85% accuracy", would try a few approaches until they get there, not ask the analyst to compare runs manually.

**What was built:** `run_goal_driven_training(X, y, problem_type, goal_metric, goal_target, model_dir, base_id)` pure function in `core/trainer.py`. It tries algorithms in priority order (linear/logistic → Random Forest → Gradient Boosting), stops early when the goal is met, and falls back to hyperparameter tuning on the best algorithm if no trial succeeds. Datasets >5,000 rows are sub-sampled for speed (trial mode). Returns `{goal_metric, goal_target, achieved, winner_algorithm, winner_algorithm_name, winner_score, trials, tried_tuning, summary}`. `_goal_score()` helper maps metric names to metrics dict keys. `_GOAL_TRIAL_ALGORITHMS` dict defines the ordered trial list per problem type. `_GOAL_TRAIN_PATTERNS` (8 NL variants: "I need 85% accuracy", "reach 0.85 R²", "hit 80% F1", "train a model until it reaches 90% accuracy", "keep trying algorithms until…", "we want 0.9 precision") added to `chat.py`. `_extract_goal_target()` helper extracts `(metric, threshold)` from a message: handles `85%` → `0.85`, `0.85` → `0.85`, defaults to `r2`/`accuracy` by problem type. Handler in `send_message()` checks `ctx["feature_set"].target_column`, applies transformations from `feature_set.transformations`, derives feature columns from `df.columns - target_col`, then fires `run_goal_driven_training()`. `{type:"goal_training"}` SSE event. `GoalTrainingCard` (emerald/amber border, 🎯): "Goal Achieved ✓" or "Best Effort" badge, goal-target badge, winner highlight box, trials table with ✓/✗, optional tuning note, summary. `GoalTrainingResult`/`GoalTrainingTrial` TypeScript types; `attachGoalTrainingToLastMessage` Zustand action.

**One bug fixed during implementation:** chat.py handler initially referenced `_fs.target_col` and `_fs.feature_cols` — neither exists on the `FeatureSet` model (it's `target_column` and feature columns are derived from the DataFrame post-transformations). Fixed by reading the field correctly and computing features as `df.columns - target_column` after applying transformations. **Testing:** 8 pattern tests + 6 extractor tests + 3 `_goal_score` unit tests + 8 pure-function tests (regression achieves goal, unreachable target, classification goal, result fields, trial fields, summary, early stop) + 3 API integration tests (event emitted, required fields present). 16 frontend tests (figure aria-label, heading, achieved/best-effort badges, goal target badge, winner name, winner score, trials table, checkmarks, crosses, tuning note absent/present, summary, all trial names). **26 backend + 16 frontend = 42 new tests. Total: 2595 backend + 1268 frontend = 3863, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend build + lint: clean.**

## Day 25 — 20:00 — Inline Multi-Feature Prediction via Chat: "run a prediction for Region=East, Units=150" (2569 backend + 1252 frontend = 3821 tests)

No community issues today. All Phase 9 Tracks D, C, and E remain complete; this session continued Track B (Vision-Driven Innovation). The chosen gap: a deployed model can only be queried through the prediction dashboard — but the vision says "Conversation over configuration. Every interaction can happen through chat." An analyst who just trained a model should be able to ask "what would revenue be for Units=100, Region=East?" right in the conversation without navigating away.

**What was built:** `_INLINE_PRED_PATTERNS` (8 NL variants: "run/make/give me a prediction for/with", "what would X be if", "score this record", "run the model on") in `chat.py`. `_KV_PAIR_RE` regex extracts `key=value`, `key: value`, `key is value` pairs from the message; `_extract_multi_feature_prediction()` normalises keys case-insensitively and via underscore↔space mapping against the model's feature list, casts numeric strings to float. Missing features fill from `pipeline.feature_means`. The handler calls `predict_single()` only when a deployment exists and the what-if handler hasn't already fired (avoiding double-prediction). `{type:"inline_prediction"}` SSE event carries prediction, probabilities (classification), confidence_interval (regression), provided_features (parsed from message), defaults_used_count, target_column, summary, and problem_type. Claude's system prompt gets the result for natural narration. `InlinePredictionCard` (blue border, 🔮): regression shows large prediction value + 95% CI; classification shows probability bars per class sorted descending; both show input badges for provided features and a defaults note when training means were used. Types, store action, SSE handler, and import all wired in page.tsx.

**One design decision:** the what-if handler changes ONE feature from training means; the inline prediction handler provides MULTIPLE explicit features. They're clearly distinct but can fire on overlapping messages (e.g. "predict with units=20"). Guarded `and not whatif_chat_event` ensures only one fires per message turn — what-if takes priority since it's the more specific single-feature analysis. **Testing:** 8 pattern tests + 6 extractor unit tests (explicit equals, case-insensitive, underscore variant, numeric conversion, unknown features excluded, empty match) + 3 API integration tests (event emitted, required fields present, provided features recorded). 15 frontend tests (regression heading, target column, prediction value formatting, CI rendering, feature badges, defaults note, plural/singular, classification probability bars, percentages, aria-label, aria-hidden icon, no CI when null, confidence badge fallback). **17 backend + 15 frontend = 32 new tests. Total: 2569 backend + 1252 frontend = 3821, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend build + lint: clean.**

## Day 25 — 12:00 — Dataset Distribution Comparison: "What changed in my data?" (2552 backend + 1246 frontend = 3798 tests)

No community issues today. All Phase 9 Tracks D, C, and E are complete and Track B continues. This session targeted the **new-data-upload gap** in the vision: when an analyst uploads a second or third dataset to an existing project — perhaps next quarter's sales data, or updated customer records — they need to know immediately if the data looks meaningfully different from what the model was trained on. A smart colleague would notice these shifts and flag them before retraining.

**What was built:** `compute_dataset_comparison(old_df, new_df)` is a pure function in `core/analyzer.py` that compares two DataFrames and returns a structured drift report. It detects: (1) **row count changes** (with ± % change); (2) **schema changes** (new columns appeared, old columns dropped); (3) **numeric distribution shifts** — for each shared numeric column, computes mean shift % and classifies severity: high (>30% shift), medium (10–30%), low (<10%); only medium/high are reported to avoid noise; (4) **categorical changes** — new categories, dropped categories, and top frequency shift (reported when ≥10%); (5) **drift score 0–100** — a weighted sum of row changes (up to 15), schema changes (up to 15), numeric drift (up to 40), and categorical drift (up to 30); (6) **plain-English summary** that classifies the severity and recommends whether to retrain. `GET /api/data/compare?baseline_id=&new_id=` endpoint loads both datasets from disk and returns the report. `_DATASET_COMPARE_PATTERNS` (9 NL variants: "what changed in my data", "distribution shift", "has my data changed", "new vs old data", "differences between uploads", etc.) detects intent in chat, finds the two most recent datasets in the project, and emits `{type:"dataset_comparison"}` SSE events with context injected into the system prompt so Claude can narrate the specific shifts. `DatasetComparisonCard` (orange border, 📊 icon): drift score badge (green <20, yellow 20–49, red ≥50), change count badge, baseline + new file info with row/column counts, row-change %, schema changes section (green for new, red for dropped), numeric drift table with arrow directions + severity badges, categorical drift rows with new/dropped category lists and frequency shift.

**One design choice:** the uniqueness filter (meant to detect ID-like columns) was initially applied to numeric columns too — that would have hidden valid numeric targets. Fixed by applying cardinality exclusion only to categorical columns. Separately, the pattern regex was overly strict with `\b` anchors causing "distribution shift" to not match; removed `\b` at the outer group boundary since the regex uses alternation groups that don't uniformly end at word boundaries.

**Testing:** 13 pure-function backend tests (zero drift for identical datasets, large shift detected, small shift not reported, new/dropped categorical categories, new/dropped columns, row count change, drift score 0 for identical, drift score high for 5× revenue, summary mentions "significant" for high drift, col count fields, empty-df guard) + 3 API integration tests (report returned, 404 on unknown, revenue shift detected) + 7 chat pattern tests (positive: 6 variants, negative: 2 unrelated phrases). 18 frontend tests (card heading, summary, baseline/new filenames, row counts, drift score badge colors, change count badge, numeric table column name, severity badge, categorical section, new/dropped categories, new/dropped schema columns, no-changes state, aria-label, row-change %, negative row change). **23 backend + 18 frontend = 41 new tests. Total: 2552 backend + 1246 frontend = 3798, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend build + lint: clean.**

## Day 25 — 04:00 — Prediction Opportunity Discovery: "What can I predict?" (2529 backend + 1228 frontend = 3757 tests)

No community issues today. All Phase 9 Tracks D, C, and E are complete. This session continued Track B (Vision-Driven Innovation) and targeted the **cold-start gap** in the vision: a business analyst who uploads their data often knows their domain but doesn't know *which column to model*. Generic ML tools say "pick a target" and leave the analyst stuck. AutoModeler can be the smart colleague who says "given your data, here are 3-5 things worth predicting and why."

**What was built:** `compute_prediction_opportunities(col_stats, row_count)` is a pure function in `core/analyzer.py` that scores every eligible dataset column as a potential prediction target. It uses three layers of logic: (1) **Exclusion filters** — ID-like columns (by name pattern `_id$`, `^pk$`, etc. or high categorical uniqueness), columns with >30% missing data, constant numeric columns, and free-text categoricals (>20 unique values) are all silently dropped; (2) **Problem type detection** — numeric columns with real variation → regression; categoricals with 2–20 unique values → classification; (3) **Scoring** — a 0-100 feasibility score rewards data completeness, predictor variety, and name-pattern business value (`revenue`/`churn` → "high", `price`/`rate` → "medium"). Results are ranked by feasibility then business value and capped at 5. `_example_question()` generates a domain-appropriate natural-language question for each opportunity ("Can you predict the Revenue for each record in my next dataset?"). `GET /api/data/{dataset_id}/prediction-opportunities` exposes the analysis. `_PREDICT_OPP_PATTERNS` (9 NL variants: "what can I predict", "what should I model", "suggest a target", "prediction opportunities", "what columns can I predict") in `chat.py` detects the intent, injects the top suggestion + full ranked list into the system prompt, and emits `{type:"prediction_opportunities"}` SSE events. `PredictionOpportunitiesCard` (purple border, 🎯 icon): count + high-value badges, ranked rows with problem-type + business-value badges, reason text, example question in quotes, feasibility score bar, and an optional "Set target" button per row.

**One key bug found and fixed during testing:** the 80% uniqueness filter (meant to catch ID columns like `user_id=1,2,3...`) was also excluding legitimate numeric targets like `revenue` (which naturally has many distinct float values). Fixed by applying the uniqueness filter only to non-numeric columns — numeric columns are never excluded for high cardinality, only for being constant or ID-named.

**Testing:** 7 pattern tests + 13 pure-function tests (regression/classification detection, high-value ranking, ID exclusion, missing-data exclusion, category exclusion, constant exclusion, max-5 cap, empty/small dataset, required fields, feasibility range, business value) + 3 API integration tests (returns opportunities, revenue in results, 404 on unknown dataset). 19 frontend tests (heading, count badge singular/plural, high-value badge, opportunity rows, problem type + business value badges, reason text, example question, feasibility score, three-opportunity rendering, aria-label, aria-hidden icon, empty returns null, Set target button + callback, no button without callback). **24 backend + 19 frontend = 43 new tests. Total: 2529 backend + 1228 frontend = 3757, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend build + lint: clean.**

## Day 24 — 20:00 — Proactive Model Health Alerts (2505 backend + 1209 frontend = 3714 tests)

No community issues today. All spec tracks (D, C, E) were complete, so this session continued Track B (Vision-Driven Innovation). The chosen feature: **proactive model health alerts on session load** — closing the "analyst has to remember to check deployment health" gap. A returning analyst who hasn't logged in for a week shouldn't have to navigate to the deployment panel to discover their model is 200 days old and needs retraining; the system should tell them.

**What was built:** `compute_deployment_health_item()` is a pure function in `core/analyzer.py` that scores a single deployment across two signals: **age** (100 if <30 days old, decreasing to 20 if >180 days) and **usage** (100 if predicted within 7 days, 40 if idle >90 days). Combined score `= age×0.55 + usage×0.45` produces a 0-100 health score; status is `healthy` (≥75), `warning` (50–74), or `critical` (<50). `top_issue` and `recommendation` are plain-English, naming the actual age in days or idle time. `compute_project_health_summary()` aggregates items for all deployments in a project, applies worst-case escalation for `overall_status`, and produces a one-sentence summary ("1 of 2 deployed models needs attention"). `GET /api/projects/{project_id}/health-summary` endpoint converts ORM objects to dicts and calls this pure function. `_HEALTH_SUMMARY_PATTERNS` (9 NL variants) in `chat.py` detects questions like "how are my models doing?" / "do I need to retrain?" and emits `{type:"health_summary"}` SSE events. **Proactive injection**: on project load, `page.tsx` calls `api.projects.healthSummary()` for returning visitors with deployments; if there are alerts, the `health_summary` is attached directly to the welcome-back message — it appears automatically, no question needed. `ProjectHealthCard` adapts its border/colors to status (emerald/amber/red), shows count badges, per-alert rows with health score bars, top issues, and "View Deployment" / "Retrain Model" CTA buttons that switch the right panel tab.

**Testing:** 7 pure-function backend tests (fresh=healthy, stale+idle=critical, age/usage scoring, name formatting, unknown algorithm fallback, empty summary, all-healthy summary, critical escalation, alerts exclude healthy items) + 2 pattern tests + 3 API integration tests (no deployments, 404 on missing project, fresh deployment returns healthy). 14 frontend tests (figure aria-label, status headings for all 3 states, deployment count badge, healthy/critical/warning badges, top_issue/recommendation display, CTA buttons, tab switch callbacks, null return for 0 deployments, multiple alert rows). **16 backend + 14 frontend = 30 new tests. Total: 2505 backend + 1209 frontend = 3714, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend build + lint: clean.**

## Day 24 — 12:00 — Conversation Export as HTML Report (2475 backend + 1195 frontend = 3670 tests)

Two Track B (Vision-Driven Innovation) sessions ran earlier today: Auto-Retrain on Upload (05:30, 14+10=24 tests) and this session's Conversation Export. This session closes the "share the full analysis journey" gap — the one piece analysts always need when presenting to a VP but couldn't do: a permanent, offline artifact of their entire exploration, modeling, and validation conversation.

**What was built:** `_CONV_EXPORT_PATTERNS` (13 NL variants: "export this conversation", "download the analysis", "share this report", "generate a report", etc.) in `chat.py` detects export intent and emits `{type:"conversation_export"}` SSE event carrying the download URL, AI message count, and dataset name. `_build_export_html(project, dataset, best_run, messages)` is a pure function that generates a fully self-contained HTML document — no external CSS, no JavaScript dependencies, prints cleanly — with a styled header (project name, date, dataset info, message count), green model results box (algorithm, primary metric, plain-English summary), and the full conversation transcript as alternating user/assistant divs (HTML-escaped content, timestamps). `GET /api/chat/{project_id}/export` wraps this and returns it as a `Content-Disposition: attachment` HTML response. Best model run is found by preferring `is_selected` then falling back to highest primary metric. Returns 404 for unknown projects. `ConversationExportCard` (emerald border, 📄 icon): message count badge, dataset name badge, description, "Download HTML Report" `<a download>` link pointing to the backend export URL. `ConversationExportInfo` TypeScript type, `attachConversationExportToLastMessage` Zustand action, SSE wired in page.tsx.

## Day 24 — 04:00 — Smart Model Selection Advisor: Goal-Criteria Ranking via Chat (2461 backend + 1165 frontend = 3626 tests)

All Phase 9 tracks (D, C, E) are done and the Model Improvement Advisor was built last session. This session's Track B work targets the complementary gap: analysts who have multiple models but don't know which one to pick. The previous session tells you *how to improve* a model; this session tells you *which model to use right now* for your specific situation.

**What was built:** `compute_model_selection(runs, criteria)` pure function in `core/advisor.py` scores every completed run across 5 analyst-facing criteria: **accuracy** (straight primary metric), **explainability** (algorithm rank inverted to 0-1: linear > logistic > decision_tree > RF > XGB > MLP > ensemble), **stability** (cross-validation CoV — lower variance = more stable), **speed** (algorithm complexity proxy), and **balanced** (0.40×acc + 0.30×expl + 0.30×stab composite). Each run gets all four component scores plus a composite score for ranking. `_ALGO_PLAIN` and `_EXPLAIN_WHY` dicts provide human-friendly algorithm names and a plain-English justification for why the winner was chosen for each algorithm. `GET /api/models/{project_id}/model-selection?criteria=` endpoint validates criteria (HTTP 400 on invalid) and returns the ranked result. `_MODEL_SELECT_PATTERNS` (15 NL variants) + `_detect_selection_criteria()` helper in `chat.py` detect "which model should I use", "most explainable model", "fastest model", etc. and extract the criteria from keywords; system prompt injection names the winner + ranking so Claude can narrate naturally. `{type:"model_selection"}` SSE event. `ModelSelectionCard` (indigo border, 🏆 icon) in chat: criteria + count badges, winner highlight box with algorithm name and plain-English justification, four component score mini-bars, ranked run list (🏆 for rank 1, selected/deployed badges), summary sentence.

**Testing:** 42 backend pure-function tests cover all scoring helpers individually (accuracy/explainability/stability/speed clamps and ordering), score_run field completeness, compute_model_selection for all 5 criteria, rank ordering, invalid criteria fallback, single-run edge case, flag preservation, and 5 API integration tests (accuracy winner, explainability winner, invalid criteria 400, unknown project 404, no-runs 404). 18 frontend tests cover rendering, criteria badge, run count badge, winner display, component score bars, ranked list, trophy emoji, is_selected/is_deployed badges, no-winner state, and aria-label. **42 backend + 18 frontend = 60 new tests. Total: 2461 backend + 1165 frontend = 3626, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend build + lint: clean.**

## Day 24 — 04:41 — Model Improvement Advisor: Ranked Actionable Suggestions via Chat (2419 backend + 1147 frontend = 3566 tests)

All Phase 9 tracks (D, C, E) were complete and no community issues were filed, so this session chose the highest-impact Track B (Vision-Driven Innovation) work: a **Model Improvement Advisor** that closes the gap between "I have a model" and "I have the best possible model."

**What was built:** `core/advisor.py` provides `compute_improvement_suggestions()` — a pure function that runs 9 independent improvement checks against the trained model's metrics, feature set, and training choices. Checks: weak features detected but not removed, ensemble methods not yet tried (when R² < 0.80), date columns unused as features, small training dataset (<2000 rows), class imbalance unhandled, calibration missing on classifiers, hyperparameter tuning not yet run, too few features (<3), and linear model on data that likely has nonlinear patterns. Each suggestion carries `difficulty` (easy/medium/hard) and `expected_impact` (high/moderate/low), sorted high-impact-first then easiest-first within each tier. `GET /api/models/{project_id}/improvement-suggestions` endpoint loads context (best run metrics, dataset size, date columns, weak feature count, calibration flag) and returns the ranked list. `_IMPROVEMENT_PATTERNS` (14 NL variants) in `chat.py` — deliberately distinct from the existing `_TUNE_PATTERNS` which is hyperparameter-only. The chat handler injects the top suggestions + current metric values into the system prompt so Claude can present them conversationally. `{type:"model_improvement"}` SSE event. `ModelImprovementCard` (violet border, 💡 icon) renders in the chat with suggestion count + metric badges, per-row category icons (🎯 features/🤖 algorithm/📊 data/⚖️ reliability), impact + difficulty badges, and explanations. Directly implements the vision's "smart colleague" promise — a colleague who proactively tells you how to get better results, not just confirms what you already did.

**Testing:** 41 backend pure-function tests cover all 9 check functions individually (trigger conditions, skip conditions, correct impact/difficulty) plus integration tests for sorting, field completeness, n_suggestions count consistency, and classification edge cases. 13 frontend tests cover rendering, badge counts, accessibility (figure/aria-label, aria-hidden icons), and the empty-suggestions state. **41 backend + 13 frontend = 54 new tests. Total: 2419 backend + 1147 frontend = 3566, all passing. Backend lint: clean. Frontend build + lint: clean.**

## Day 23 — 20:00 — VP-Quality Prediction Page UX: 5 Friction Fixes (2378 backend + 1134 frontend = 3512 tests)

This session closes the final two Track E (End-to-End Polish) items: the "lunch break flow audit" and the "shareable prediction page UX." A code audit of the full analyst journey (upload → explore → train → deploy → share) identified 5 friction points concentrated in the VP-facing `predict/[id]` page — the link the analyst emails to their boss.

**Friction point 1 — Generic title**: "Prediction Dashboard" tells a VP nothing. Fixed: page title now dynamically reads `"{Target Column} Predictor"` (e.g., "Revenue Predictor") from `deployment.target_column`. The VP immediately knows what the model predicts before scrolling.

**Friction point 2 — No model trust context**: The predict page had algorithm and problem-type badges but no plain-English context. Fixed: new `ModelContextCard` shows algorithm in plain English via `algoName()` mapping ("random_forest_regressor" → "Random Forest"), accuracy phrased as "Explains 84% of variation (good)" for regression or "92% accuracy on training data" for classification, and deployment date. This gives a VP the three questions they ask before trusting any number: what method was used, how accurate is it, and how fresh is it.

**Friction point 3 — Cryptic feature labels and missing hints**: Numeric fields showed "(numeric)" but no guidance.
